\xce\xa1\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Sigma" title="Sigma">\n          \xce\xa3\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Tau" title="Tau">\n          \xce\xa4\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Upsilon" title="Upsilon">\n          \xce\xa5\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Phi" title="Phi">\n          \xce\xa6\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Chi_(letter)" title="Chi (letter)">\n          \xce\xa7\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Psi_(letter)" title="Psi (letter)">\n          \xce\xa8\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Omega" title="Omega">\n          \xce\xa9\n         </a>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th colspan="33">\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lower_case" title="Lower case">\n          lower case\n         </a>\n        </th>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         \xce\xb1\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         \xce\xb2\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         \xce\xb3\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         \xce\xb4\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         \xce\xb5\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         \xce\xb6\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         \xce\xb7\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         \xce\xb8\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         \xce\xb9\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         \xce\xba\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         \xce\xbb\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         \xce\xbc\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         \xce\xbd\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         \xce\xbe\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         \xce\xbf\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         \xcf\x80\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         \xcf\x81\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         \xcf\x83\n         <br/>\n         \xcf\x82\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         \xcf\x84\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         \xcf\x85\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         \xcf\x86\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         \xcf\x87\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         \xcf\x88\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         \xcf\x89\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Diacritics">\n        Diacritics\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greek_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Diacritics">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Greek_diacritics" title="Greek diacritics">\n        Greek diacritics\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In addition to the letters, the Greek alphabet features a number of\n       <a href="/wiki/Diacritic" title="Diacritic">\n        diacritical signs\n       </a>\n       : three different accent marks (\n       <a href="/wiki/Acute_accent" title="Acute accent">\n        acute\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Grave_accent" title="Grave accent">\n        grave\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Circumflex" title="Circumflex">\n        circumflex\n       </a>\n       ), originally denoting different shapes of\n       <a href="/wiki/Pitch_accent" title="Pitch accent">\n        pitch accent\n       </a>\n       on the stressed vowel; the so-called breathing marks (\n       <a href="/wiki/Rough_breathing" title="Rough breathing">\n        rough\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Smooth_breathing" title="Smooth breathing">\n        smooth breathing\n       </a>\n       ), originally used to signal presence or absence of word-initial /h/; and the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trema_(diacritic)" title="Trema (diacritic)">\n        diaeresis\n       </a>\n       , used to mark full syllabic value of a vowel that would otherwise be read as part of a diphthong. These marks were introduced during the course of the Hellenistic period. Actual usage of the grave in\n       <a href="/wiki/Penmanship" title="Penmanship">\n        handwriting\n       </a>\n       saw a rapid decline in favor of uniform usage of the acute during the late 20th century, and it has only been retained in\n       <a href="/wiki/Typography" title="Typography">\n        typography\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       After the writing reform of 1982, most diacritics are no longer used. Since then, Greek has been written mostly in the simplified\n       <a href="/wiki/Greek_diacritics" title="Greek diacritics">\n        monotonic orthography\n       </a>\n       (or monotonic system), which employs only the acute accent and the diaeresis. The traditional system, now called the polytonic orthography (or polytonic system), is still used internationally for the writing of\n       <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek" title="Ancient Greek">\n        Ancient Greek\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Punctuation">\n        Punctuation\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greek_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Punctuation">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       In Greek, the question mark is written as the English semicolon, while the functions of the colon and semicolon are performed by a raised point (\xe2\x80\xa2), known as the\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Interpunct#Ano_teleia" title="Interpunct">\n         ano teleia\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       (\n       <span lang="grc" xml:lang="grc">\n        \xce\xac\xce\xbd\xcf\x89 \xcf\x84\xce\xb5\xce\xbb\xce\xb5\xce\xaf\xce\xb1\n       </span>\n       ). In Greek the\n       <a href="/wiki/Comma" title="Comma">\n        comma\n       </a>\n       also functions as a\n       <a href="/wiki/Silent_letter" title="Silent letter">\n        silent letter\n       </a>\n       in a handful of Greek words, principally distinguishing\n       <span lang="el" xml:lang="el">\n        <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%CF%8C,%CF%84%CE%B9" title="wikt:\xcf\x8c,\xcf\x84\xce\xb9">\n         \xcf\x8c,\xcf\x84\xce\xb9\n        </a>\n       </span>\n       (\n       <i>\n        \xc3\xb3,ti\n       </i>\n       , "whatever") from\n       <span lang="el" xml:lang="el">\n        <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%CF%8C%CF%84%CE%B9" title="wikt:\xcf\x8c\xcf\x84\xce\xb9">\n         \xcf\x8c\xcf\x84\xce\xb9\n        </a>\n       </span>\n       (\n       <i>\n        \xc3\xb3ti\n       </i>\n       , "that").\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">\n        <a href="#cite_note-32">\n         [32]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Ancient Greek texts often used\n       <i>\n        scriptio continua\n       </i>\n       (\'continuous writing\'), which means that ancient authors and scribes would write word after word with no spaces or punctuation between words to differentiate or mark boundaries.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">\n        <a href="#cite_note-33">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Latin_alphabet">\n        Latin alphabet\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greek_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Latin alphabet">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Greek has occasionally been written in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Latin_script" title="Latin script">\n        Latin script\n       </a>\n       , especially in areas under\n       <a href="/wiki/Stato_da_M%C3%A0r" title="Stato da M\xc3\xa0r">\n        Venetian rule\n       </a>\n       or by\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_Greece" title="Roman Catholicism in Greece">\n        Greek Catholics\n       </a>\n       . The term\n       <span lang="grc" xml:lang="grc">\n        <i>\n         Frankolevantinika\n        </i>\n        / \xce\xa6\xcf\x81\xce\xb1\xce\xb3\xce\xba\xce\xbf\xce\xbb\xce\xb5\xce\xb2\xce\xb1\xce\xbd\xcf\x84\xce\xaf\xce\xbd\xce\xb9\xce\xba\xce\xb1\n       </span>\n       applies when the Latin script is used to write Greek in the cultural ambit of Catholicism (because\n       <span lang="grc" xml:lang="grc">\n        <i>\n         Frankos\n        </i>\n        / \xce\xa6\xcf\x81\xce\xac\xce\xb3\xce\xba\xce\xbf\xcf\x82\n       </span>\n       is an older Greek term for\n       <i>\n        Roman Catholic\n       </i>\n       ).\n       <span lang="grc" xml:lang="grc">\n        <i>\n         Frankochiotika\n        </i>\n        / \xce\xa6\xcf\x81\xce\xb1\xce\xb3\xce\xba\xce\xbf\xcf\x87\xce\xb9\xcf\x8e\xcf\x84\xce\xb9\xce\xba\xce\xb1\n       </span>\n       (meaning "Catholic Chiot") alludes to the significant presence of Catholic missionaries based on the island of\n       <a href="/wiki/Chios" title="Chios">\n        Chios\n       </a>\n       . Additionally the term\n       <a href="/wiki/Greeklish" title="Greeklish">\n        Greeklish\n       </a>\n       is often used when the Greek language is written in a Latin script in online communications.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">\n        <a href="#cite_note-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" The dative/locative of Ancient Greek disappeared in the late Hellenistic period, and the instrumental case of Mycenaean Greek disappeared in the Archaic period.\n         </span>\n        </li>\n        <li id="cite_note-22">\n         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">\n          <b>\n           <a href="#cite_ref-22">\n            ^\n           </a>\n          </b>\n         </span>\n         <span class="reference-text">\n          There is no particular morphological form that can be identified as \'subjunctive\' in the modern language, but the term is sometimes encountered in descriptions even if the most complete modern grammar (Holton et al. 1997) does not use it and calls certain traditionally-\'subjunctive\' forms \'dependent\'. Most Greek linguists advocate abandoning the traditional terminology (Anna Roussou and Tasos Tsangalidis 2009, in\n          <i>\n           Meletes gia tin Elliniki Glossa\n          </i>\n          , Thessaloniki, Anastasia Giannakidou 2009 "Temporal semantics and polarity: The dependency of the subjunctive revisited", Lingua); see\n          <a href="/wiki/Modern_Greek_grammar#The_verb" title="Modern Greek grammar">\n           Modern Greek grammar\n          </a>\n          for explanation.\n         </span>\n        </li>\n        <li id="cite_note-23">\n         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">\n          <b>\n           <a href="#cite_ref-23">\n            ^\n           </a>\n          </b>\n         </span>\n         <span class="reference-text">\n          <a href="#CITEREFBeekes2009">\n           Beekes 2009\n          </a>\n          .\n         </span>\n        </li>\n        <li id="cite_note-24">\n         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">\n          <b>\n           <a href="#cite_ref-24">\n            ^\n           </a>\n          </b>\n         </span>\n         <span class="reference-text">\n          <a href="#CITEREFScheler1977">\n           Scheler 1977\n          </a>\n          .\n         </span>\n        </li>\n        <li id="cite_note-25">\n         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">\n          <b>\n           <a
